# Task | Update coding question pool with new questions for 288 tenant

### Description

+++ Question 1 ( Easy )

You are given an array of integers that may contain both **active markers** (non-zero) and **inactive markers** (represented by `0`). Rearrange the array so that all active markers stay in their original **relative order**, while all inactive markers (`0`) are shifted to the **end** of the array.

**Examples:**Â 

***Input**: arr\[\] = \[1, 2, 0, 4, 3, 0, 5, 0\]*
***Output**: \[1, 2, 4, 3, 5, 0, 0, 0\]*
***Explanation**: There are three 0s that are moved to the end.*

***Input**: arr\[\] = \[10, 20, 30\]*
***Output**: \[10, 20, 30\]*
***Explanation**: No change in array as there are no 0s.*

***Input**: arr\[\] = \[0, 0\]*
***Output**: \[0, 0\]*
***Explanation**: No change in array as there are all 0s.*

*Code*

```
function moveZerosToEnd(arr) {
  if (!Array.isArray(arr) || arr.length === 0) return arr;

  let j = 0; // write index for next non-zero
  for (let i = 0; i < arr.length; i++) {
    if (arr[i] !== 0) {
      arr[j++] = arr[i];
    }
  }

  // fill remaining positions with 0
  while (j < arr.length) {
    arr[j++] = 0;
  }

  return arr; // array modified in-place
}
Test cases. 
```

+++

+++ Question 2 ( Easy )

You are given an array of integers that is **already sorted in ascending order**.
Your task is to **rearrange the array in-place** (do not use extra space for another array) so that the numbers follow a **zig-zag pattern**.

In other words, every even-indexed element should be greater than or equal to its adjacent odd-indexed elements (if they exist).

**Note:** The given array is sorted in ascending order, and modify the given array in-place without returning a new array.

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5\]*
***Output:** \[2, 1, 4, 3, 5\]*
***Explanation:** Array elements after sorting it in the waveform are 2, 1, 4, 3, 5.*

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[2, 4, 7, 8, 9, 10\]*
***Output:** \[4, 2, 8, 7, 10, 9\]*
***Explanation:** Array elements after sorting it in the waveform are 4, 2, 8, 7, 10, 9.*

*Code*

```
function zigzagWave(arr) {
  if (!Array.isArray(arr) || arr.length < 2) return arr;
  for (let i = 0; i + 1 < arr.length; i += 2) {
    // swap arr[i] and arr[i+1]
    [arr[i], arr[i + 1]] = [arr[i + 1], arr[i]];
  }
  return arr; // modified in-place
}Test cases:
```

+++

+++ Question 3 ( Easy )

Youâre provided with an integer array of size `n` containing both non-negative and negative values.
Rearrange the numbers so that they **alternate between non-negative and negative values**, beginning with a non-negative.
Maintain the **original sequence order** of positives and negatives.

If there are extra numbers of one type, append them at the end.
Consider `0` as non-negative.

**Note:** The rearranged array should start with a positive number and 0 (zero) should be considered as a positive number.

**Examples:**Â 

***Input**: Â arr\[\] = \[1, 2, 3, -4, -1, 4\]*
***Output**: arr\[\] = \[1, -4, 2, -1, 3, 4\]*

***Input**: Â arr\[\] = \[-5, -2, 5, 2, 4, 7, 1, 8, 0, -8\]*
***Output**: arr\[\] = \[5, -5, 2, -2, 4, -8, 7, 1, 8, 0\]*

*Code*

```
function rearrangeAlternating(arr) {
  const positives = [];
  const negatives = [];

  // Partition while preserving order (0 is considered non-negative)
  for (const x of arr) {
    if (x >= 0) positives.push(x);
    else negatives.push(x);
  }

  let i = 0, p = 0, q = 0;
  // Alternate starting with a non-negative
  while (p < positives.length && q < negatives.length) {
    arr[i++] = positives[p++];
    arr[i++] = negatives[q++];
  }

  // Append remaining positives (if any)
  while (p < positives.length) arr[i++] = positives[p++];

  // Append remaining negatives (if any)
  while (q < negatives.length) arr[i++] = negatives[q++];

  return arr; // array mutated in-place, also returned for convenience
}Test cases
```

+++

+++ Question 4 ( Easy )

You are given an array of integers.
We define a **"dominant element"** as a number that is **greater than or equal to every element that comes after it** in the array.
By definition, the last element is always dominant since no values follow it.

Write a program to collect all such dominant elements from left to right.

**Note:** The leftmost element is always a leader.

**Examples:**

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[16, 17, 4, 3, 5, 2\]*
***Output:** \[17 5 2\]*
***Explanation:** 17 is greater than all the elements to its right i.e., \[4, 3, 5, 2\], therefore 17 is a leader. 5 is greater than all the elements to its right i.e., \[2\], therefore 5 is a leader. 2 has no element to its right, therefore 2 is a leader.*

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 2\]*
***Output:** \[5 2\]*
***Explanation:** 5 is greater than all the elements to its right i.e., \[2\], therefore 5 is a leader. 2 has no element to its right, therefore 2 is a leader.*

*Code* 

```
function dominantElements(arr) {
  if (!Array.isArray(arr) || arr.length === 0) return [];

  const leaders = [];
  let maxSoFar = -Infinity;

  for (let i = arr.length - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
    if (arr[i] >= maxSoFar) {
      leaders.push(arr[i]);
      maxSoFar = arr[i];
    }
  }

  // leaders are collected from right to left, so reverse to return left-to-right
  return leaders.reverse();
}
Test cases
```

+++

+++ Question 5 ( Easy )

You are given an array of numbers and a positive integer `k`.
Rearrange the array by **reversing every block of** `k` consecutive elements in place.
If the final block contains fewer than `k` elements, simply reverse that smaller block as well.

The array must be updated directly (no return of a new array).

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8\], k = 3*
***Output:** \[3, 2, 1, 6, 5, 4, 8, 7\]*
***Explanation:** Elements is reversed: \[1, 2, 3\] â \[3, 2, 1\], \[4, 5, 6\] â \[6, 5, 4\], and the last group \[7, 8\](size < 3) is reversed as \[8, 7\].*

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5\], k = 3*
*Output: \[3, 2, 1, 5, 4\]*
*Explanation: First group consists of elements 1, 2, 3. Second group consists of 4, 5.*

*I**nput:** arr\[\] = \[5, 6, 8, 9\], k = 5*
***Output:** \[9, 8, 6, 5\]*
***Explanation:** Since k is greater than array size, the entire array is reversed.*

*Code* 

```
function reverseBlocks(arr, k) {
  if (!Array.isArray(arr) || arr.length === 0) return;
  if (k <= 0) return; // assume k is positive per problem, but guard anyway

  const n = arr.length;
  for (let i = 0; i < n; i += k) {
    let l = i;
    let r = Math.min(i + k - 1, n - 1);
    while (l < r) {
      [arr[l], arr[r]] = [arr[r], arr[l]];
      l++; r--;
    }
  }
  // array is modified in-place; returning it is optional
  return arr;
}Test cases
```

+++ Question 6 ( Easy )

You are given an **inclusive interval** `[low, high]` and a sorted array of unique integers inside this interval.
A number is said to be **"absent"** if it belongs to `[low, high]` but does not appear in the array.

Your task is to produce the **minimum set of continuous ranges** that together cover all absent numbers, such that:

* No number from the input array is inside any of these ranges.
* Every absent number is included exactly once.

Return the list of ranges in sorted order.

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[14, 15, 20, 30, 31, 45\], lower = 10, upper = 50*
***Output:** \[\[10, 13\], \[16, 19\], \[21, 29\], \[32, 44\], \[46, 50\]\]*
***Explanation:** These ranges represent all missing numbers between 10 and 50 not present in the array*

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[-48, -10, -6, -4, 0, 4, 17\], lower = -54, upper = 17*
***Output:** \[\[-54, -49\], \[-47, -11\], \[-9, -7\], \[-5, -5\], \[-3, -1\], \[1, 3\], \[5,16\]\]*
***Explanation:** These ranges represent all missing numbers between -54 and 17 not present in the array.*

*code*

```
function findMissingRanges(arr, lower, upper) {
  const res = [];
  let prev = lower - 1;

  for (let i = 0; i <= arr.length; i++) {
    // use sentinel at the end to handle the final gap up to upper
    const curr = i < arr.length ? arr[i] : upper + 1;

    if (curr - prev >= 2) {
      res.push([prev + 1, curr - 1]);
    }

    prev = curr;
  }

  return res;
}
Test cases
```

+++

+++ Question 7 ( Medium )

You are given an array of **positive integers** and a number `K`.
Your task is to count the **total number of contiguous subarrays** whose **product of elements is strictly less than K**.

The subarrays must consist of **consecutive** elements from the array, and each valid subarray should be counted exactly once.

***Input :** arr\[\] = \[1, 2, 3, 4\]Â *
*Â  Â  Â  Â  Â  Â  K = 10*
***Output :** 7*
*The subarrays are {1}, {2}, {3}, {4}, {1, 2}, {1, 2, 3} and {2, 3}*

***Input Â :** arr\[\] = \[1, 9, 2, 8, 6, 4, 3\]Â *
*Â  Â  Â  Â  Â  Â  Â K = 100*
***Output :** 16*

***Input Â :** arr\[\] = \[10, 5, 2, 6\] Â *
*Â  Â  Â  Â  Â  Â  Â K = 100*
***Output :** 8*

*Code* 

```
function countSubarraysProductLessThanK(arr, K) {
  if (K <= 1) return 0; // with positive integers, no product < K if K <= 1
  let prod = 1;
  let left = 0;
  let count = 0;

  for (let right = 0; right < arr.length; right++) {
    prod *= arr[right];

    while (prod >= K && left <= right) {
      prod /= arr[left];
      left++;
    }

    // All subarrays ending at 'right' starting from left..right are valid
    count += (right - left + 1);
  }

  return count;
}Test case
```

+++

+++ Question 8 ( Medium )

You are given the **available time intervals** of two people as two separate lists of non-overlapping intervals.
Each interval is represented as `[start, end]` and no interval within a list overlaps with another.

Given a **meeting duration** `d`, find the **earliest overlapping interval** between the two people that is at least `d` long.

Return the interval as `[start, start + d]`. If no such interval exists, return an empty array.

***Input: slt1\[\]\[\]** = \[\[10,50\], \[60,120\], \[140,210\]\], **slt2\[\]\[\]** = \[\[0,15\], \[60,70\]\], d = 8*
***Output:** \[60,68\]*
***Explanation**: The only overlap is \[60,70\] (10 minutes), which is enough for an 8-minute meeting, so answer is \[60,68\]*

***Input: slt1\[\]\[\]** = \[\[10,50\], \[60,120\], \[140,210\]\], **slt2\[\]\[\]** = \[\[0,15\], \[60,70\]\], d = 12*
***Output:** \[\]*
***Explanation:** The only overlap is \[60, 70\] (10 minutes), but 12 minutes are needed, so no valid slot exists.*

*Code* 

```
function earliestMeetingSlot(slots1, slots2, d) {
  let i = 0, j = 0;
  while (i < slots1.length && j < slots2.length) {
    const start = Math.max(slots1[i][0], slots2[j][0]);
    const end = Math.min(slots1[i][1], slots2[j][1]);

    if (end - start >= d) {
      return [start, start + d];
    }

    // move the pointer with the smaller end time
    if (slots1[i][1] < slots2[j][1]) i++;
    else j++;
  }
  return [];
}Test cases
```

+++

+++ Question 9 ( Medium )

You are given an array of integers.
Your task is to find a **contiguous segment** of the array that yields the **maximum sum possible**, and return that sum.

A segment must contain at least one element, and all elements in the segment are consecutive in the original array.

`Input`***:** arr\[\] = \[2, 3, -8, 7, -1, 2, 3\]*
***Output:** 11*
***Explanation:** The subarray \[7, -1, 2, 3\] has the largest sum 11.*

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[-2, -4\]*
***Output:** -2*
***Explanation:** The subarray \[-2\] has the largest sum -2.*

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[5, 4, 1, 7, 8\]*
***Output:** 25*
***Explanation:** The subarray \[5, 4, 1, 7, 8\] has the largest sum 25.*

*Code*

```
function maxSubarraySum(arr) {
  if (!arr || arr.length === 0) return 0; // or throw depending on spec

  // Initialize with first element to handle all-negative arrays
  let maxEndingHere = arr[0];
  let maxSoFar = arr[0];

  for (let i = 1; i < arr.length; i++) {
    const x = arr[i];
    // extend previous subarray or start new at current element
    maxEndingHere = Math.max(x, maxEndingHere + x);
    // update global maximum
    maxSoFar = Math.max(maxSoFar, maxEndingHere);
  }

  return maxSoFar;
}
Test cases
```

+++ Question 10 ( Medium )

You are given an array consisting only of **0's and 1's**.
Your task is to find the **minimum number of swaps** required to bring all the **1's** **together in a contiguous block**.

* A swap can exchange **any two elements** in the array.
* If there are **no 1's in the array**, return `-1`.

***Examples:**Â **Input:** arr\[\] = \[1, 0, 1, 0, 1\]*
***Output:** 1*
***Explanation:** Only 1 swap is required to group all 1's together. Swapping index 1 with 4 will *
* give arr\[\] = \[1, 1, 1, 0, 0\]*
**
***Input:** arr\[\] = \[1, 1, 0, 1, 0, 1, 1\]*
***Output:** 2*
***Explanation:** Only 2 swap is required to group all 1's together. Swapping index 0 with 2 and *
*1 with 4 will give arr\[\] = \[0, 0, 1, 1, 1, 1, 1\]*

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[0, 0, 0\]*
***Output:** -1*
***Explanation:** No 1s are present in the array, so return -1.*

*Code*

```
function minSwapsToGroupOnes(arr) {
  const n = arr.length;
  // total number of ones
  const k = arr.reduce((s, x) => s + (x === 1 ? 1 : 0), 0);
  if (k === 0) return -1;       // no 1s present
  if (k === n) return 0;        // already all 1s

  // count ones in the initial window [0..k-1]
  let onesInWindow = 0;
  for (let i = 0; i < k; i++) {
    if (arr[i] === 1) onesInWindow++;
  }

  let maxOnes = onesInWindow;

  // slide the window
  for (let i = k; i < n; i++) {
    if (arr[i] === 1) onesInWindow++;
    if (arr[i - k] === 1) onesInWindow--;
    if (onesInWindow > maxOnes) maxOnes = onesInWindow;
  }

  // minimum swaps = zeros in best window = k - maxOnes
  return k - maxOnes;
}Test cases
```

+++ Question 11 ( Medium )

You are given an array of integers.

Your task is to find all **elements that appear more than** `ân/3â` times in the array, where `n` is the size of the array.

Return the **sorted list of such elements**. If no element satisfies the condition, return an empty array.

**Note**: The returned array of majority elements should be sorted.

**Examples:**

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[2, 2, 3, 1, 3, 2, 1, 1\]*
***Output:** \[1, 2\]*
***Explanation:** The frequency of 1 and 2 is 3, which is more than floor n/3 (8/3 = 2).*

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[-5, 3, -5\]*
***Output:** \[-5\]*
***Explanation:** The frequency of -5 is 2, which is more than floor n/3 (3/3 = 1).*

***Input:** arr\[\] = \[3, 2, 2, 4, 1, 4\]*
***Output:** \[ \]*
***Explanation:** There is no majority element.*

*Code* 

```
function majorityElements(nums) {
  if (!nums || nums.length === 0) return [];

  // 1) Find up to two candidates
  let cand1 = null, cand2 = null;
  let cnt1 = 0, cnt2 = 0;

  for (const x of nums) {
    if (cand1 !== null && x === cand1) {
      cnt1++;
    } else if (cand2 !== null && x === cand2) {
      cnt2++;
    } else if (cnt1 === 0) {
      cand1 = x; cnt1 = 1;
    } else if (cnt2 === 0) {
      cand2 = x; cnt2 = 1;
    } else {
      cnt1--; cnt2--;
    }
  }

  // 2) Verify actual counts
  cnt1 = 0; cnt2 = 0;
  for (const x of nums) {
    if (x === cand1) cnt1++;
    else if (x === cand2) cnt2++;
  }

  // 3) Collect results > floor(n/3), sort before returning
  const res = [];
  const threshold = Math.floor(nums.length / 3);
  if (cnt1 > threshold) res.push(cand1);
  if (cand2 !== cand1 && cnt2 > threshold) res.push(cand2);

  return res.sort((a, b) => a - b);
}Test cases
```

+++ Question 12 ( Medium )

We are given an array consisting of n elements. At each operation we can select any one element and **increase rest of n-1 elements by 1**. We have to make all elements equal performing such operation as many times you wish. Find the **minimum** number of operations needed for this.

**Examples:**Â 

*I**nput:** arr\[\] = \[1, 2, 3\]*
***Output:** 3*
***Explanation:** *
*Operation 1 : Increase all except 3rd, we get 2, 3, 3*
*Operation 2 : Increase all except 3rd, we get 3, 4, 3*
*Operation 3 : Increase all except 2nd, we get 4, 4, 4*
**
***Input:** arr\[\] = \[4, 3, 4\]*
***Output:** 2*
***Explanation:***
*Operation 1 : Increase all except 3rd, we get 5, 4, 4*
*Operation 2 : Increase all except 1st, we get 5, 5, 5*

Code

```
function minOperationsToEqualize(arr) {
  if (!arr || arr.length === 0) return 0;
  let sum = 0;
  let min = Infinity;
  for (const x of arr) {
    sum += x;
    if (x < min) min = x;
  }
  return sum - min * arr.length;
}
```

+++

+++ Question 13 ( Medium )

You are given an array of distinct integers. Your goal is to **reorder the elements** to produce the **next arrangement in dictionary order**. If the current arrangement is already the **highest possible**, rearrange it into the **lowest possible order** (sorted in ascending order). Return the array after performing this transformation.

**Example 1:**
Input: `[2, 4, 1, 7, 5, 0]`
Output: `[2, 4, 5, 0, 1, 7]`

**Example 2:**
Input: `[3, 2, 1]`
Output: `[1, 2, 3]`

**Example 3:**
Input: `[1, 3, 5, 4, 2]`
Output: `[1, 4, 2, 3, 5]`

Code

```
function nextPermutation(arr) {
  const n = arr.length;
  if (n <= 1) return arr;

  // find pivot i
  let i = n - 2;
  while (i >= 0 && arr[i] >= arr[i + 1]) i--;

  if (i >= 0) {
    // find j to swap with pivot
    let j = n - 1;
    while (arr[j] <= arr[i]) j--;
    // swap
    [arr[i], arr[j]] = [arr[j], arr[i]];
  }

  // reverse suffix i+1 .. n-1
  let l = i + 1, r = n - 1;
  while (l < r) {
    [arr[l], arr[r]] = [arr[r], arr[l]];
    l++; r--;
  }

  return arr;
}
```

+++

+++ Question 14 ( Hard )

You are given an array of integers arranged in a **looped (circular) fashion**, meaning the element after the last one is the first element. Your goal is to determine the **maximum sum of any non-empty contiguous segment**, where the segment can either lie entirely within the array or wrap around the end back to the beginning. Return the maximum sum that can be achieved.

**Example 1:**
Input: `[8, -8, 9, -9, 10, -11, 12]`
Output: `22`

**Example 2:**
Input: `[4, -1, -2, 3]`
Output: `7`

**Example 3:**
Input: `[5, -2, 3, 4]`
Output: `12`

Code - 

```
function maxSubarrayCircular(arr) {
  if (!arr || arr.length === 0) return 0;

  let total = arr[0];
  let maxEnding = arr[0], maxSoFar = arr[0];
  let minEnding = arr[0], minSoFar = arr[0];

  for (let i = 1; i < arr.length; i++) {
    const x = arr[i];
    maxEnding = Math.max(x, maxEnding + x);
    maxSoFar = Math.max(maxSoFar, maxEnding);

    minEnding = Math.min(x, minEnding + x);
    minSoFar = Math.min(minSoFar, minEnding);

    total += x;
  }

  // If all numbers are negative, maxSoFar is the largest (least negative) number,
  // and total === minSoFar (min subarray is the entire array). Wrapping is invalid.
  if (total === minSoFar) return maxSoFar;

  return Math.max(maxSoFar, total - minSoFar);
}
```

+++

+++ Question 15 ( Hard )

You are given `K` lists of integers, each sorted in ascending order. Your task is to identify the smallest continuous range of integers `[min, max]` such that the range contains at least one number from each of the K lists.

* If multiple ranges have the same size, return the one with the **smallest starting number**.

**Example 1:**
Input: `[[4,7,9,12,15],[0,8,10,14,20],[6,12,16,30,50]]`
Output: `[6,8]`

**Example 2:**
Input: `[[2,4],[1,7],[20,40]]`
Output: `[4,20]`

**Example 3:**
Input: `[[1,5,9],[2,6,10],[3,7,11]]`
Output: `[3,5]`

Solution

```
function smallestRange(lists) {
  const k = lists.length;
  if (k === 0) return [];
  for (const lst of lists) if (!lst || lst.length === 0) return [];

  // Flatten with origin index
  const arr = [];
  for (let i = 0; i < k; i++) {
    for (const v of lists[i]) arr.push([v, i]);
  }

  // Sort by value
  arr.sort((a, b) => a[0] - b[0]);

  const count = new Array(k).fill(0);
  let have = 0, left = 0;
  let bestLen = Infinity, bestL = 0, bestR = 0;

  for (let right = 0; right < arr.length; right++) {
    const [valR, idxR] = arr[right];
    if (count[idxR] === 0) have++;
    count[idxR]++;

    // Try to shrink from the left while all lists are represented
    while (have === k && left <= right) {
      const valL = arr[left][0];
      const currLen = valR - valL;
      if (currLen < bestLen || (currLen === bestLen && valL < bestL)) {
        bestLen = currLen;
        bestL = valL;
        bestR = valR;
      }

      // Move left pointer
      const idxL = arr[left][1];
      count[idxL]--;
      if (count[idxL] === 0) have--;
      left++;
    }
  }

  return [bestL, bestR];
}
```

+++

+++ Question 16 ( Hard )

You are given a positive integer `n`. Your task is to:

1. Reverse the digits of `n` to form a new number `rev`.
2. Compute the number obtained by raising `n` to the power of `rev` (i.e., `n^rev`).

Return the resulting number.

**Example 1:**
Input: `2`
Output: `4`
Explanation: Reverse of `2` is `2`. `2^2 = 4`.

**Example 2:**
Input: `10`
Output: `10000000000` (i.e., `10^1 = 10`)
Explanation: Reverse of `10` is `01` â considered as `1`. `10^1 = 10`.

Code

```
function reverseStringTrimLeadingZeros(s) {
  const rev = s.split('').reverse().join('');
  // Remove leading zeros after reversal; if all zeros, return "0"
  const trimmed = rev.replace(/^0+/, '');
  return trimmed === '' ? '0' : trimmed;
}

function powBigInt(base, exp) {
  // fast exponentiation with BigInt exponent
  let b = BigInt(base);
  let e = BigInt(exp);
  let result = 1n;
  while (e > 0n) {
    if (e & 1n) result *= b;
    b *= b;
    e >>= 1n;
  }
  return result;
}

function powerWithReversed(n) {
  const s = String(n);
  const revStr = reverseStringTrimLeadingZeros(s);
  const base = BigInt(s);
  const exponent = BigInt(revStr);
  const res = powBigInt(base, exponent);
  // return as string to avoid precision/display issues for very large numbers
  return res.toString();
}
```

Test cases

+++

+++ Question 17 ( Hard )

You are given a string `s` and a list of valid words `dictionary`. Your task is to determine whether `s` can be split into a sequence of one or more dictionary words. Words must be **used exactly as in the dictionary** and concatenated to form `s`.

Return `true` if such a segmentation exists, otherwise return `false`.

**Example 1:**
Input: `s = "ilike"`, `dictionary = ["i", "like", "gfg"]`
Output: `true`
Explanation: The string can be segmented as `"i like"`.

**Example 2:**
Input: `s = "ilikegfg"`, `dictionary = ["i", "like", "man", "india", "gfg"]`
Output: `true`
Explanation: The string can be segmented as `"i like gfg"`.

**Example 3:**
Input: `s = "ilikemangoes"`, `dictionary = ["i", "like", "gfg"]`
Output: `false`
Explanation: No valid segmentation exists.

Code

```
function wordBreak(s, dictionary) {
  const n = s.length;
  const dict = new Set(dictionary);
  let maxLen = 0;
  for (const w of dictionary) maxLen = Math.max(maxLen, w.length);

  const dp = new Array(n + 1).fill(false);
  dp[0] = true;

  for (let i = 1; i <= n; i++) {
    const start = Math.max(0, i - maxLen);
    for (let j = i - 1; j >= start; j--) {
      if (!dp[j]) continue;
      if (dict.has(s.slice(j, i))) {
        dp[i] = true;
        break;
      }
    }
  }
  return dp[n];
}
```

+++ Question 18 ( Hard )

You are given an array of integers `arr[]` and two integers `l` and `r`. Your task is to **count the number of contiguous subarrays** in which the **maximum element lies within the range** `[l, r]`, inclusive.

Return the count of such valid subarrays.

**Example 1:**
Input: `arr = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5], l = 2, r = 5`
Output: `11`
Explanation: Subarrays like `[2], [3], [2,3], [1,2,3]` etc., have maximum in the range `[2,5]`.

**Example 2:**
Input: `arr = [3, 1, 6, 4], l = 3, r = 6`
Output: `9`

**Example 3:**
Input: `arr = [1, 2, 3, 4], l = 5, r = 7`
Output: `0`

Answer

```
function countSubarrays(arr, l, r) {
  const countAtMost = (bound) => {
    let cur = 0; // length of current segment with all elements <= bound
    let total = 0;
    for (let x of arr) {
      if (x <= bound) {
        cur += 1;
        total += cur;
      } else {
        cur = 0;
      }
    }
    return total;
  };

  return countAtMost(r) - countAtMost(l - 1);
}
```

+++

+++ Question 19 ( Hard )

At a party, there are `n` people labeled from `0` to `n-1`. You are given a square matrix `mat` of size `n x n` where:

* `mat[i][j] == 1` means person `i` knows person `j`.
* `mat[i][j] == 0` means person `i` does not know person `j`.

A **celebrity** is someone who **everyone knows**, but who **does not know anyone else** (except themselves).

Write a program to find the index of the celebrity if one exists. If there is no celebrity, return `-1`.

**Constraints:**

* `mat[i][i] == 1` for all `i`.

**Example 1:**
Input: `[[1,1,0],[0,1,0],[0,1,1]]`
Output: `1`

**Example 2:**
Input: `[[1,1],[1,1]]`
Output: `-1`

**Example 3:**
Input: `[[1]]`
Output: `0`

Answer

```
function findCelebrity(mat) {
  const n = mat.length;
  if (n === 0) return -1;

  // Find candidate
  let a = 0, b = n - 1;
  while (a < b) {
    if (mat[a][b] === 1) {
      // a knows b -> a cannot be celebrity
      a++;
    } else {
      // a doesn't know b -> b cannot be celebrity
      b--;
    }
  }
  const c = a;

  // Verify candidate
  for (let i = 0; i < n; i++) {
    if (i === c) continue;
    // celebrity should not know others, and everyone should know celebrity
    if (mat[c][i] === 1 || mat[i][c] === 0) return -1;
  }
  return c;
}
```

```
    "category": "Stress",
    "description": "20x20 stress case forming a circular 'knows' chain (each person knows themselves and the next person). No one is known by everyone => no celebrity (-1). Tests performance on larger input with no celebrity.",
    "score": 15,
    "weightage": 15
  }
]
```

+++

+++ Question 20 ( Hard )

You are given a string `str` consisting of **lowercase letters** and the characters `'('` and `')'`. Your task is to **remove the minimum number of parentheses** to make the string **balanced**, where:

* Every opening parenthesis `'('` must have a matching closing parenthesis `')'`.
* No closing parenthesis should appear without a matching opening parenthesis.

Return **all distinct balanced strings** obtainable by performing the **minimum number of removals**.

**Example 1:**
Input: `"()())()"`
Output: `"()()()" "(())()"`

**Example 2:**
Input: `"(v)())()"`
Output: `"(v)()()" "(v())()"`

**Example 3:**
Input: `")("`
Output: `""`

Solution:

```
/**
 * @param {string} s
 * @return {string[]}
 */
function removeInvalidParentheses(s) {
    const isValid = (str) => {
        let count = 0;
        for (let ch of str) {
            if (ch === '(') count++;
            else if (ch === ')') {
                if (count === 0) return false;
                count--;
            }
        }
        return count === 0;
    };

    const res = [];
    const visited = new Set();
    const queue = [s];
    let found = false;

    while (queue.length > 0) {
        const levelSize = queue.length;
        const levelVisited = new Set();

        for (let i = 0; i < levelSize; i++) {
            const str = queue.shift();

            if (isValid(str)) {
                res.push(str);
                found = true;
            }

            if (found) continue; // Only collect valid strings at minimum removal

            for (let j = 0; j < str.length; j++) {
                if (str[j] !== '(' && str[j] !== ')') continue;
                const next = str.slice(0, j) + str.slice(j + 1);
                if (!visited.has(next)) {
                    queue.push(next);
                    visited.add(next);
                }
            }
        }

        if (found) break; // Stop BFS once minimum removals found
    }

    // If no valid strings found, return empty string
    return res.length > 0 ? [...new Set(res)] : [""];
}

// Example usage:
console.log(removeInvalidParentheses("()())()")); // ["()()()", "(())()"]
console.log(removeInvalidParentheses("(v)())()")); // ["(v)()()", "(v())()"]
console.log(removeInvalidParentheses(")(")); // [""]
```
